# Kimi Guided Story Image Request

Date: 2026-05-24

Generate illustration-only assets for these inactive Guided Story drafts. Do not embed text in any image.

## Global Rules

- No embedded text, captions, labels, watermarks, or speech bubbles.
- Kimi is an asset renderer, not the story author.
- Kimi must follow Codex story text, character bibles, environment bibles, and page prompts exactly.
- Kimi must never improvise story details, rewrite app text, paraphrase narration, or add new events.
- Kimi must never redesign characters.
- Kimi must never alter clothing randomly.
- Kimi must never alter environments randomly.
- Kimi must never change time of day, weather, lighting, species, age, body proportions, or recurring props unless the exact page text requires it.
- Kimi must never add embedded text, labels, captions, watermarks, or speech bubbles.
- Kimi must preserve visual continuity across every page of each fiction book.
- Fiction continuity is mandatory. A beautiful image still fails if character, clothing, setting, lighting, weather, props, or art style drift.
- All pages of a book must look like the same illustrated universe.
- Character drift is forbidden.
- Random redesigns are forbidden.
- Every page prompt must reference the canonical character bible and environment bible.
- Every page must be generated with awareness of the previous page and the story sequence.
- Keep character age/species, clothing, colors, hair/fur, accessories, body proportions, and setting details consistent across every page of the same book.
- Do not add random extra characters.
- Do not randomly change time of day, weather, lighting, buildings, props, or background location.
- Do not activate or approve fiction pages that fail continuity checks.
- Avoid scary, violent, or intense imagery.
- Use a warm, child-friendly, modern illustration style.
- Compose images so the main action is readable on mobile.
- Match the exact app text and required action for each page.

## gs-c-01: The Lion and the Little Mouse

- Level: C
- Source: The Lion and the Mouse (Aesop's Fables)
- Source type: public_domain_adaptation
- Status: draft_needs_assets

### Character Bible
- Luma the lion
  - canonical appearance: golden adult lion with a soft brown mane, amber eyes, broad paws, and calm gentle posture
  - age/species: adult lion
  - skin/fur/body color: golden fur with a warm brown mane
  - hair/mane/head detail: full soft brown mane, same shape on every page
  - eye color/style: amber eyes
  - clothing: no clothing
  - accessories: no accessories
  - personality: powerful but gentle, surprised at first, grateful by the end
  - speaking style: slow, warm, respectful
  - height/build/proportions: large sturdy lion with broad paws and consistent adult proportions
  - setting relationship: belongs in the same sunny grassland near one shady tree
- Pip the mouse
  - canonical appearance: small gray mouse with round ears, black eyes, pink nose, and a tiny blue scarf
  - age/species: small mouse
  - skin/fur/body color: soft gray fur with pale pink inner ears and nose
  - hair/mane/head detail: smooth gray head fur with round ears
  - eye color/style: small black eyes
  - clothing: tiny blue scarf only
  - accessories: tiny blue scarf, always tied the same way
  - personality: brave, polite, determined, kind
  - speaking style: small but clear and brave
  - height/build/proportions: tiny rounded mouse, always much smaller than Luma
  - setting relationship: lives near the grassland tree and small mouse hole

### Environment Bible
- primary setting: sunny grassland near a shady tree
- time of day: Use the same time-of-day logic from the story sequence; do not change randomly.
- weather: Use stable weather unless the page text clearly changes it.
- lighting: Keep lighting coherent from page to page unless the story intentionally changes time.
- recurring props: none specified
- setting continuity: Each page must feel like it belongs to the same story world and sequence.
- forbidden setting drift: random desert, beach, classroom, city, or indoor switch unless written in the page text; random season changes; random weather changes; random day/night changes; unexplained new buildings, props, or background characters

### Continuity Status
- draft_needs_assets
- Fiction continuity is mandatory. Reject/regenerate any page with character drift, clothing drift, setting drift, weather/lighting drift, or disconnected narrative sequencing.

### Page Image Requirements
### Page 1
- Exact app text: Luma the lion slept under a warm tree. Pip the mouse ran over his paw and stopped with a squeak.
- Required visible characters: Luma the lion, Pip the mouse
- Required setting: warm grassland under a tree
- Required action: Luma sleeping while Pip freezes beside his paw

Environment bible: primary setting is sunny grassland near a shady tree; time/weather/lighting must remain coherent with previous pages. Continuity rule: this page must visually follow page 1 as the opening scene; do not redesign characters, clothing, props, setting, lighting, or art style. No embedded text, captions, labels, watermarks, speech bubbles, or extra characters. Keep character age/species, clothing, colors, and accessories identical to the character bible.
- Forbidden: embedded text, captions, speech bubbles, watermarks, random extra characters, random character redesigns, random clothing changes, random setting, weather, or lighting changes, scary or violent imagery
- Continuity checklist: same character appearance, same clothing and accessories, same hair/fur/body colors, same visual age/species/body proportions, same illustration style, logical setting continuity, coherent time of day/weather/lighting, recurring props remain consistent, story events flow in page order
- Previous-page continuity rule: Generate this page as the next scene in the same illustrated book. Compare it to prior pages before finalizing.
- Consistency notes: Luma the lion: golden adult lion with a soft brown mane, amber eyes, broad paws, and calm gentle posture Pip the mouse: small gray mouse with round ears, black eyes, pink nose, and a tiny blue scarf

## gs-c-02: The Crow and the Water Jar

- Level: C
- Source: The Crow and the Pitcher (Aesop's Fables)
- Source type: public_domain_adaptation
- Status: draft_needs_assets

### Character Bible
- Cora the crow
  - canonical appearance: black crow with glossy feathers, dark eyes, charcoal beak, and a tiny green leaf tucked near one wing
  - age/species: adult crow
  - skin/fur/body color: glossy black feathers with subtle blue highlights
  - hair/mane/head detail: smooth black head feathers
  - eye color/style: dark brown eyes
  - clothing: no clothing
  - accessories: tiny green leaf tucked near the same wing on every page
  - personality: thirsty, thoughtful, patient, proud of a good plan
  - speaking style: clear and thoughtful
  - height/build/proportions: small bird with consistent crow proportions
  - setting relationship: moves around the same dry garden path and clay jar
- Little sparrow
  - canonical appearance: small tan sparrow with a cream belly, tiny brown beak, and bright black eyes
  - age/species: small sparrow
  - skin/fur/body color: tan feathers with cream belly
  - hair/mane/head detail: smooth tan head feathers
  - eye color/style: bright black eyes
  - clothing: no clothing
  - accessories: no accessories
  - personality: curious and impressed
  - speaking style: short cheerful chirps
  - height/build/proportions: smaller than Cora, round sparrow body
  - setting relationship: watches from the same garden wall near the jar

### Environment Bible
- primary setting: dry garden path with a clay water jar
- time of day: Use the same time-of-day logic from the story sequence; do not change randomly.
- weather: Use stable weather unless the page text clearly changes it.
- lighting: Keep lighting coherent from page to page unless the story intentionally changes time.
- recurring props: none specified
- setting continuity: Each page must feel like it belongs to the same story world and sequence.
- forbidden setting drift: random desert, beach, classroom, city, or indoor switch unless written in the page text; random season changes; random weather changes; random day/night changes; unexplained new buildings, props, or background characters

### Continuity Status
- draft_needs_assets
- Fiction continuity is mandatory. Reject/regenerate any page with character drift, clothing drift, setting drift, weather/lighting drift, or disconnected narrative sequencing.

### Page Image Requirements
### Page 1
- Exact app text: Cora the crow flew over a dry garden. Her throat felt scratchy, and she looked for water.
- Required visible characters: Cora the crow
- Required setting: dry garden
- Required action: Cora flying over a dry garden path
- Image prompt: Book: The Crow and the Water Jar. Page 1. Exact app text: "Cora the crow flew over a dry garden. Her throat felt scratchy, and she looked for water." Environment bible: primary setting is dry garden path with a clay water jar; time/weather/lighting must remain coherent with previous pages. - Continuity checklist: same character appearance, same clothing and accessories, same hair/fur/body colors, same visual age/species/body proportions, same illustration style, logical setting continuity, coherent time of day/weather/lighting, recurring props remain consistent, story events flow in page order
- Previous-page continuity rule: Generate this page as the next scene in the same illustrated book. Compare it to prior pages before finalizing.
- Consistency notes: Cora the crow: black crow with glossy feathers, dark eyes, charcoal beak, and a tiny green leaf tucked near one wing Little sparrow: small tan sparrow with a cream belly, tiny brown beak, and bright black eyes

### Page 2
- Exact app text: She found a tall clay jar beside a wall. Cora hopped close and saw water far down inside.
- Required visible characters: Cora the crow
- Required setting: garden wall
- Required action: Cora peering into a tall clay jar

## gs-c-03: The Fox and the High Grapes

- Level: C
- Source: The Fox and the Grapes (Aesop's Fables)
- Source type: public_domain_adaptation
- Status: draft_needs_assets

### Character Bible
- Felix the fox
  - canonical appearance: small red fox with orange-red fur, white tail tip, amber eyes, and a tan satchel
  - age/species: young fox
  - skin/fur/body color: orange-red fur with cream chest and white tail tip
  - hair/mane/head detail: smooth red fox head fur with pointed ears
  - eye color/style: amber eyes
  - clothing: no clothing
  - accessories: tan satchel worn across one shoulder, same placement every page
  - personality: eager, embarrassed, then honest
  - speaking style: quick and proud at first, softer when honest
  - height/build/proportions: small slim fox with consistent pointed ears and bushy tail
  - setting relationship: walks beneath the same grape vine and vineyard fence
- Fence bird
  - canonical appearance: small blue bird with a yellow chest, round black eyes, and short tail feathers
  - age/species: small bird
  - skin/fur/body color: blue feathers with yellow chest
  - hair/mane/head detail: smooth blue head feathers
  - eye color/style: round black eyes
  - clothing: no clothing
  - accessories: no accessories
  - personality: observant and gentle
  - speaking style: light, curious, kind
  - height/build/proportions: tiny bird, always much smaller than Felix
  - setting relationship: perches on the same vineyard fence near the grapes

### Environment Bible
- primary setting: vineyard with a high grape vine
- time of day: Use the same time-of-day logic from the story sequence; do not change randomly.
- weather: Use stable weather unless the page text clearly changes it.
- lighting: Keep lighting coherent from page to page unless the story intentionally changes time.
- recurring props: none specified
- setting continuity: Each page must feel like it belongs to the same story world and sequence.
- forbidden setting drift: random desert, beach, classroom, city, or indoor switch unless written in the page text; random season changes; random weather changes; random day/night changes; unexplained new buildings, props, or background characters

### Continuity Status
- draft_needs_assets
- Fiction continuity is mandatory. Reject/regenerate any page with character drift, clothing drift, setting drift, weather/lighting drift, or disconnected narrative sequencing.

## gs-c-04: The Dog and the River Shadow

- Level: C
- Source: The Dog and His Shadow (Aesop's Fables)
- Source type: public_domain_adaptation
- Status: draft_needs_assets

### Character Bible
- Rex the dog
  - canonical appearance: brown dog with floppy ears, warm brown eyes, short tail, and a red collar
  - age/species: friendly medium-sized dog
  - skin/fur/body color: warm brown fur with slightly darker floppy ears
  - hair/mane/head detail: short smooth brown head fur
  - eye color/style: warm brown eyes
  - clothing: no clothing
  - accessories: red collar, always the same
  - personality: proud, tempted, disappointed, then wiser
  - speaking style: expressed through dog body language, no spoken dialogue
  - height/build/proportions: medium dog with sturdy body and floppy ears
  - setting relationship: walks from the village path across the same small river bridge
- Baker Mara
  - canonical appearance: kind adult baker with medium brown skin, gray-streaked dark hair in a bun, white apron, and blue dress
  - age/species: adult human baker
  - skin/fur/body color: medium brown skin
  - hair/mane/head detail: dark hair with gray streaks, always tied in a bun
  - eye color/style: dark brown eyes
  - clothing: white apron over a simple blue dress
  - accessories: small flour cloth tucked at apron side
  - personality: kind, observant, calm
  - speaking style: gentle and practical
  - height/build/proportions: average-height adult with steady posture
  - setting relationship: belongs to the village path near the bakery and bridge

### Environment Bible
- primary setting: small bridge over a calm river
- time of day: Use the same time-of-day logic from the story sequence; do not change randomly.
- weather: Use stable weather unless the page text clearly changes it.
- lighting: Keep lighting coherent from page to page unless the story intentionally changes time.
- recurring props: none specified
- setting continuity: Each page must feel like it belongs to the same story world and sequence.
- forbidden setting drift: random desert, beach, classroom, city, or indoor switch unless written in the page text; random season changes; random weather changes; random day/night changes; unexplained new buildings, props, or background characters

### Continuity Status
- draft_needs_assets
- Fiction continuity is mandatory. Reject/regenerate any page with character drift, clothing drift, setting drift, weather/lighting drift, or disconnected narrative sequencing.

  - clothing: Use the same clothing on every page; if no clothing is specified, do not add random clothing.
  - accessories: Use only the accessories named in the canonical appearance, and keep them unchanged.

  - speaking style: Use natural child-friendly dialogue that matches the character's role.

### Character Bible

## gs-d-04: Two Mice, Two Homes

- Level: D
- Source: The Town Mouse and the Country Mouse (Aesop's Fables)
- Source type: public_domain_adaptation
- Status: draft_needs_assets

### Character Bible
- Milo the country mouse
  - canonical appearance: tan mouse with a straw hat and green vest
  - age/species: tan mouse with a straw hat and green vest
  - skin/fur/body color: Use the exact skin, fur, feather, or body color named in the canonical appearance; if not visible, keep it visually unchanged.
  - hair/mane/head detail: Use the exact hair, mane, feather, or head detail named in the canonical appearance; if not applicable, do not invent one.
  - eye color/style: Use one consistent eye color and eye style across every page.
  - clothing: Use the same clothing on every page; if no clothing is specified, do not add random clothing.
  - accessories: Use only the accessories named in the canonical appearance, and keep them unchanged.
  - personality: Keep the character's emotional role consistent with the story arc.
  - speaking style: Use natural child-friendly dialogue that matches the character's role.
  - height/build/proportions: Keep the same size, body shape, proportions, and visual age across every page.
  - setting relationship: Keep the character visually connected to the story setting and sequence.
- Tilly the town mouse
  - canonical appearance: gray mouse with a purple capelet and tiny silver satchel
  - age/species: gray mouse with a purple capelet and tiny silver satchel
  - skin/fur/body color: Use the exact skin, fur, feather, or body color named in the canonical appearance; if not visible, keep it visually unchanged.
  - hair/mane/head detail: Use the exact hair, mane, feather, or head detail named in the canonical appearance; if not applicable, do not invent one.
  - eye color/style: Use one consistent eye color and eye style across every page.
  - clothing: Use the same clothing on every page; if no clothing is specified, do not add random clothing.
  - accessories: Use only the accessories named in the canonical appearance, and keep them unchanged.
  - personality: Keep the character's emotional role consistent with the story arc.
  - speaking style: Use natural child-friendly dialogue that matches the character's role.
  - height/build/proportions: Keep the same size, body shape, proportions, and visual age across every page.
  - setting relationship: Keep the character visually connected to the story setting and sequence.

### Environment Bible
- primary setting: country cottage and busy town kitchen
- time of day: Use the same time-of-day logic from the story sequence; do not change randomly.
- weather: Use stable weather unless the page text clearly changes it.
- lighting: Keep lighting coherent from page to page unless the story intentionally changes time.
- recurring props: none specified
- setting continuity: Each page must feel like it belongs to the same story world and sequence.
- forbidden setting drift: random desert, beach, classroom, city, or indoor switch unless written in the page text; random season changes; random weather changes; random day/night changes; unexplained new buildings, props, or background characters

### Continuity Status

- Fiction continuity is mandatory. Reject/regenerate any page with character drift, clothing drift, setting drift, weather/lighting drift, or disconnected narrative sequencing.

## gs-e-02: Golda and the Three Bowls

- Level: E
- Source: Goldilocks and the Three Bears (English Fairy Tales / traditional)
- Source type: public_domain_adaptation
- Status: draft_needs_assets

### Character Bible
- Golda
  - canonical appearance: child with light brown skin, curly golden-brown hair, teal coat, and red boots
  - age/species: child with light brown skin, curly golden-brown hair, teal coat, and red boots
  - skin/fur/body color: Use the exact skin, fur, feather, or body color named in the canonical appearance; if not visible, keep it visually unchanged.
  - hair/mane/head detail: Use the exact hair, mane, feather, or head detail named in the canonical appearance; if not applicable, do not invent one.
  - eye color/style: Use one consistent eye color and eye style across every page.
  - clothing: Use the same clothing on every page; if no clothing is specified, do not add random clothing.
  - accessories: Use only the accessories named in the canonical appearance, and keep them unchanged.
  - personality: Keep the character's emotional role consistent with the story arc.
  - speaking style: Use natural child-friendly dialogue that matches the character's role.
  - height/build/proportions: Keep the same size, body shape, proportions, and visual age across every page.
  - setting relationship: Keep the character visually connected to the story setting and sequence.
- Bear family
  - canonical appearance: three gentle brown bears wearing simple cream aprons
  - age/species: three gentle brown bears wearing simple cream aprons
  - skin/fur/body color: Use the exact skin, fur, feather, or body color named in the canonical appearance; if not visible, keep it visually unchanged.
  - hair/mane/head detail: Use the exact hair, mane, feather, or head detail named in the canonical appearance; if not applicable, do not invent one.
  - eye color/style: Use one consistent eye color and eye style across every page.
  - clothing: Use the same clothing on every page; if no clothing is specified, do not add random clothing.
  - accessories: Use only the accessories named in the canonical appearance, and keep them unchanged.
  - personality: Keep the character's emotional role consistent with the story arc.
  - speaking style: Use natural child-friendly dialogue that matches the character's role.
  - height/build/proportions: Keep the same size, body shape, proportions, and visual age across every page.
  - setting relationship: Keep the character visually connected to the story setting and sequence.

### Environment Bible
- primary setting: cozy forest cottage
- time of day: Use the same time-of-day logic from the story sequence; do not change randomly.
- weather: Use stable weather unless the page text clearly changes it.
- lighting: Keep lighting coherent from page to page unless the story intentionally changes time.
- recurring props: none specified
- setting continuity: Each page must feel like it belongs to the same story world and sequence.
- forbidden setting drift: random desert, beach, classroom, city, or indoor switch unless written in the page text; random season changes; random weather changes; random day/night changes; unexplained new buildings, props, or background characters

### Continuity Status
- draft_needs_assets
- Fiction continuity is mandatory. Reject/regenerate any page with character drift, clothing drift, setting drift, weather/lighting drift, or disconnected narrative sequencing.

### Character Bible

### Character Bible
- Ori
  - canonical appearance: gray young swan with soft feathers, dark beak, and gentle eyes
  - age/species: gray young swan with soft feathers, dark beak, and gentle eyes

### Character Bible
- Jack
  - canonical appearance: child with tan skin, straight black hair, patched green jacket, and brown boots
  - age/species: child with tan skin, straight black hair, patched green jacket, and brown boots

### Character Bible

## gs-f-04: Hare and Hedgehog at the Field

- Level: F
- Source: The Hare and the Hedgehog (Grimm fairy tales)
- Source type: public_domain_adaptation
- Status: draft_needs_assets

### Character Bible
- Hattie Hedgehog
  - canonical appearance: small hedgehog with brown spines, round glasses, and a yellow vest
  - age/species: small hedgehog with brown spines, round glasses, and a yellow vest
  - skin/fur/body color: Use the exact skin, fur, feather, or body color named in the canonical appearance; if not visible, keep it visually unchanged.
  - hair/mane/head detail: Use the exact hair, mane, feather, or head detail named in the canonical appearance; if not applicable, do not invent one.
  - eye color/style: Use one consistent eye color and eye style across every page.
  - clothing: Use the same clothing on every page; if no clothing is specified, do not add random clothing.
  - accessories: Use only the accessories named in the canonical appearance, and keep them unchanged.
  - personality: Keep the character's emotional role consistent with the story arc.
  - speaking style: Use natural child-friendly dialogue that matches the character's role.
  - height/build/proportions: Keep the same size, body shape, proportions, and visual age across every page.
  - setting relationship: Keep the character visually connected to the story setting and sequence.
- Henri Hedgehog
  - canonical appearance: small hedgehog with brown spines, blue cap, and green scarf

### Environment Bible
- primary setting: long field with two furrows
- time of day: Use the same time-of-day logic from the story sequence; do not change randomly.
- weather: Use stable weather unless the page text clearly changes it.
- lighting: Keep lighting coherent from page to page unless the story intentionally changes time.
- recurring props: none specified
- setting continuity: Each page must feel like it belongs to the same story world and sequence.
- forbidden setting drift: random desert, beach, classroom, city, or indoor switch unless written in the page text; random season changes; random weather changes; random day/night changes; unexplained new buildings, props, or background characters

## gs-c-06: The Bell in the Tree

- Level: C
- Source: Original LiteracyPath fable (LiteracyPath original guided stories)
- Source type: original
- Status: draft_needs_assets

### Character Bible
- Mina
  - canonical appearance: young child with warm brown skin, straight black bob haircut, brown eyes, red sweater, denim pants, and yellow rain boots
  - age/species: young child
  - skin/fur/body color: warm brown skin
  - hair/mane/head detail: straight black bob haircut, same length every page
  - eye color/style: brown eyes
  - clothing: red sweater, denim pants, yellow rain boots
  - accessories: no accessories
  - personality: careful, caring, curious, learns from a small mistake
  - speaking style: gentle and clear
  - height/build/proportions: small child with consistent K-2 age proportions
  - setting relationship: cares for the school garden and the bell tree
- Taro
  - canonical appearance: small white dog with one brown ear, black nose, round dark eyes, and a blue collar
  - age/species: small dog
  - skin/fur/body color: white fur with one brown ear
  - hair/mane/head detail: short smooth dog fur
  - eye color/style: round dark eyes
  - clothing: no clothing
  - accessories: blue collar, always the same
  - personality: playful, easily distracted, happy to return
  - speaking style: dog body language, no spoken dialogue
  - height/build/proportions: small compact dog, always below Mina's knees
  - setting relationship: plays in and around Mina's school garden

### Environment Bible
- primary setting: school garden with a bell hanging in a tree
- time of day: Use the same time-of-day logic from the story sequence; do not change randomly.
- weather: Use stable weather unless the page text clearly changes it.
- lighting: Keep lighting coherent from page to page unless the story intentionally changes time.
- recurring props: none specified
- setting continuity: Each page must feel like it belongs to the same story world and sequence.
- forbidden setting drift: random desert, beach, classroom, city, or indoor switch unless written in the page text; random season changes; random weather changes; random day/night changes; unexplained new buildings, props, or background characters

### Continuity Status
- draft_needs_assets
- Fiction continuity is mandatory. Reject/regenerate any page with character drift, clothing drift, setting drift, weather/lighting drift, or disconnected narrative sequencing.

## gs-e-06: The Lantern Path

- Level: E
- Source: Original LiteracyPath fable (LiteracyPath original guided stories)
- Source type: original
- Status: draft_needs_assets

### Character Bible
- Ila
  - canonical appearance: child with warm brown skin, short curly hair, mustard coat, and round lantern
  - age/species: child with warm brown skin, short curly hair, mustard coat, and round lantern
  - skin/fur/body color: Use the exact skin, fur, feather, or body color named in the canonical appearance; if not visible, keep it visually unchanged.
  - hair/mane/head detail: Use the exact hair, mane, feather, or head detail named in the canonical appearance; if not applicable, do not invent one.
  - eye color/style: Use one consistent eye color and eye style across every page.
  - clothing: Use the same clothing on every page; if no clothing is specified, do not add random clothing.
  - accessories: Use only the accessories named in the canonical appearance, and keep them unchanged.
  - personality: Keep the character's emotional role consistent with the story arc.
  - speaking style: Use natural child-friendly dialogue that matches the character's role.
  - height/build/proportions: Keep the same size, body shape, proportions, and visual age across every page.
  - setting relationship: Keep the character visually connected to the story setting and sequence.
- Mr. Vale
  - canonical appearance: older neighbor with pale skin, gray beard, navy coat, and wooden cane
  - age/species: older neighbor with pale skin, gray beard, navy coat, and wooden cane
  - skin/fur/body color: Use the exact skin, fur, feather, or body color named in the canonical appearance; if not visible, keep it visually unchanged.
  - hair/mane/head detail: Use the exact hair, mane, feather, or head detail named in the canonical appearance; if not applicable, do not invent one.
  - eye color/style: Use one consistent eye color and eye style across every page.
  - clothing: Use the same clothing on every page; if no clothing is specified, do not add random clothing.
  - accessories: Use only the accessories named in the canonical appearance, and keep them unchanged.
  - personality: Keep the character's emotional role consistent with the story arc.
  - speaking style: Use natural child-friendly dialogue that matches the character's role.
  - height/build/proportions: Keep the same size, body shape, proportions, and visual age across every page.
  - setting relationship: Keep the character visually connected to the story setting and sequence.

### Environment Bible
- primary setting: hill village during a stormy evening
- time of day: Use the same time-of-day logic from the story sequence; do not change randomly.
- weather: Use stable weather unless the page text clearly changes it.
- lighting: Keep lighting coherent from page to page unless the story intentionally changes time.
- recurring props: none specified
- setting continuity: Each page must feel like it belongs to the same story world and sequence.
- forbidden setting drift: random desert, beach, classroom, city, or indoor switch unless written in the page text; random season changes; random weather changes; random day/night changes; unexplained new buildings, props, or background characters

### Continuity Status
- draft_needs_assets
- Fiction continuity is mandatory. Reject/regenerate any page with character drift, clothing drift, setting drift, weather/lighting drift, or disconnected narrative sequencing.

### Page Image Requirements
### Page 1
- Exact app text: Rain fell hard on the hill village, and the path grew dark before supper. Ila lit the round lantern that hung by her door.
- Required visible characters: Ila
- Required setting: rainy village hill
- Required action: Ila lighting lantern at doorway

## gs-f-06: The Fox and the Rain Jar

- Level: F
- Source: Original LiteracyPath fable (LiteracyPath original guided stories)
- Source type: original
- Status: draft_needs_assets

### Character Bible
- Rafi Fox
  - canonical appearance: red fox with white paws, amber eyes, and a blue seed pouch
  - age/species: red fox with white paws, amber eyes, and a blue seed pouch
  - skin/fur/body color: Use the exact skin, fur, feather, or body color named in the canonical appearance; if not visible, keep it visually unchanged.
  - hair/mane/head detail: Use the exact hair, mane, feather, or head detail named in the canonical appearance; if not applicable, do not invent one.
  - eye color/style: Use one consistent eye color and eye style across every page.
  - clothing: Use the same clothing on every page; if no clothing is specified, do not add random clothing.
  - accessories: Use only the accessories named in the canonical appearance, and keep them unchanged.
  - personality: Keep the character's emotional role consistent with the story arc.
  - speaking style: Use natural child-friendly dialogue that matches the character's role.
  - height/build/proportions: Keep the same size, body shape, proportions, and visual age across every page.
  - setting relationship: Keep the character visually connected to the story setting and sequence.
- Momo Mole
  - canonical appearance: small brown mole with round glasses and a green digging apron
  - age/species: small brown mole with round glasses and a green digging apron
  - skin/fur/body color: Use the exact skin, fur, feather, or body color named in the canonical appearance; if not visible, keep it visually unchanged.
  - hair/mane/head detail: Use the exact hair, mane, feather, or head detail named in the canonical appearance; if not applicable, do not invent one.
  - eye color/style: Use one consistent eye color and eye style across every page.
  - clothing: Use the same clothing on every page; if no clothing is specified, do not add random clothing.
  - accessories: Use only the accessories named in the canonical appearance, and keep them unchanged.
  - personality: Keep the character's emotional role consistent with the story arc.
  - speaking style: Use natural child-friendly dialogue that matches the character's role.
  - height/build/proportions: Keep the same size, body shape, proportions, and visual age across every page.
  - setting relationship: Keep the character visually connected to the story setting and sequence.
- Lark
  - canonical appearance: small tan bird with a yellow chest and bright black eyes
  - age/species: small tan bird with a yellow chest and bright black eyes
  - skin/fur/body color: Use the exact skin, fur, feather, or body color named in the canonical appearance; if not visible, keep it visually unchanged.
  - hair/mane/head detail: Use the exact hair, mane, feather, or head detail named in the canonical appearance; if not applicable, do not invent one.

  - setting relationship: Keep the character visually connected to the story setting and sequence.

### Environment Bible
- primary setting: dry woodland garden waiting for rain
- time of day: Use the same time-of-day logic from the story sequence; do not change randomly.
- weather: Use stable weather unless the page text clearly changes it.
- lighting: Keep lighting coherent from page to page unless the story intentionally changes time.
- recurring props: none specified
- setting continuity: Each page must feel like it belongs to the same story world and sequence.
- forbidden setting drift: random desert, beach, classroom, city, or indoor switch unless written in the page text; random season changes; random weather changes; random day/night changes; unexplained new buildings, props, or background characters

### Continuity Status
- draft_needs_assets
- Fiction continuity is mandatory. Reject/regenerate any page with character drift, clothing drift, setting drift, weather/lighting drift, or disconnected narrative sequencing.
